1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Compliance Audit: Kafka Audit Logging and Authorization Events

## Your Task

Find all Java source files in `apache/kafka` that produce audit log entries for authorization decisions. Search `core/src/main/scala/` and `clients/src/main/java/` for files that log `ALLOWED` or `DENIED` authorization events, reference `AuditLogger`, or implement audit trail functionality for ACL decisions. Report the file path and the class name producing audit events.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the compliance domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/kafka--0753c489, sg-evals/flink--0cc95fcc, sg-evals/camel--1006f047.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/kafka--0753c489` (apache/kafka)
- `sg-evals/flink--0cc95fcc` (apache/flink)
- `sg-evals/camel--1006f047` (apache/camel)

## Output Format

Create a file at `/workspace/answer.json` with your findings in the following structure:

```json
{
  "files": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go"}
  ],
  "symbols": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "SymbolName"}
  ],
  "chain": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "FunctionName"}
  ],
  "text": "Narrative explanation of your findings, citing repos and file paths."
}
```

Include only the fields relevant to this task. Your answer is evaluated against a closed-world oracle — completeness matters.

## Evaluation

Your answer will be scored on:
- **File recall and precision**: Did you find all relevant files?

## Summary

I have successfully identified all Java source files in the Apache Kafka repository that produce audit log entries for authorization decisions. Here are my findings:

### Primary Audit Logging Files:

1. **StandardAuthorizerData.java** (`metadata/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/metadata/authorizer/StandardAuthorizerData.java`)
   - **Class**: `StandardAuthorizerData`
   - **Audit Logger**: Uses `LoggerFactory.getLogger("kafka.authorizer.logger")`
   - **Key Methods**:
     - `authorize()` (lines 228-252): Performs authorization and triggers audit logging
     - `logAuditMessage()` (lines 281-310): Logs authorization decisions
       - ALLOWED results logged at DEBUG level (when `logIfAllowed()` is true)
       - DENIED results logged at INFO level (when `logIfDenied()` is true)
     - `buildAuditMessage()` (lines 254-271): Constructs detailed audit messages with principal, operation, resource, host, and ACL rule information

2. **StandardAuthorizer.java** (`metadata/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/metadata/authorizer/StandardAuthorizer.java`)
   - **Class**: `StandardAuthorizer`
   - Implements the `ClusterMetadataAuthorizer` interface
   - Delegates authorization decisions to `StandardAuthorizerData`
   - Records authorization metrics

### Supporting Infrastructure:

- **Action.java** (`clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/server/authorizer/Action.java`): Provides `logIfAllowed()` and `logIfDenied()` flags to control which authorization decisions are logged

The answer has been created at `/workspace/answer.json` with complete details about files, symbols, and the audit logging call chain.

}\\n310:     }\\n311: \\n312:     private MatchingRule findAclRule(\\n313:         Set<KafkaPrincipal> matchingPrincipals,\\n314:         String host,\\n315:         Action action\\n316:     ) {\\n317:         // This code relies on the ordering of StandardAcl within the NavigableMap.\\n318:         // Entries are sorted by resource type first, then REVERSE resource name.\\n319:         // Therefore, we can find all the applicable ACLs by starting at\\n320:         // (resource_type, resource_name) and stepping forwards until we reach\\n321:         // an ACL with a resource name which // For example, when trying to authorize a TOPIC resource named foobar, we would\\n326:         // start at element 2, and continue on to 3 and 4 following map:\\n327:         //\\n328:         // 1. // Once we reached element 5, we would jump to element 7.\\n338:         MatchingRuleBuilder matchingRuleBuilder = new MatchingRuleBuilder(noAclRule);\\n339:         StandardAcl exemplar = new {\\n350:             return matchingRuleBuilder.build();\\n351:         }\\n352: \\n353:         // In addition to ACLs for this specific resource name, there can also be wildcard\\n354:         // ACLs that match any resource name. These are stored as type = LITERAL,\\n355:         // name = \\\"*\\\". We search these next.\\n356:         exemplar = new StandardAcl(\\n357:             action.resourcePattern().resourceType(),\\n358:             WILDCARD,\\n359:             LITERAL,\\n360: matchingPrincipals, host, matchingRuleBuilder);\\n365:         return matchingRuleBuilder.build();\\n366:     }\\n367: \\n368:     static int matchesUpTo(\\n369:         String resource,\\n370:             if (resource.charAt(i) != pattern.charAt(i)) break;\\n377:             i++;\\n378:         }\\n379:         return i;\\n380:     }\\n381: \\n382:     private void checkSection(\\n383: If any DENY ACLs match, the operation is denied, no matter how\n224:      * many ALLOW ACLs match. If neither ALLOW nor DENY ACLs match, we return the default\n225:      * result. In general it makes more sense to configure the default result to be\n226:      * DENY, but some people (and unit tests) configure it as ALLOW.\n227:      */\n228:     public AuthorizationResult authorize(\n229:         AuthorizableRequestContext requestContext,\n230:         Action action\n231:     ) {\n232:         if (action.resourcePattern().patternType() != LITERAL) {\n233:             throw new IllegalArgumentException(\"Only literal resources are supported. If false, no access is actually granted, the result is used\n291:                 // only to determine authorized operations. So log only at trace level.\n292:                 if (action.logIfAllowed() && auditLog.isDebugEnabled()) {\n293:                     auditLog.debug(buildAuditMessage(principal, requestContext, action, rule));\n294:                 } else if (auditLog.isTraceEnabled()) {\n295:                     auditLog.trace(buildAuditMessage(principal, requestContext, action, rule));\n296:                 }\n297:                 return;\n298: \n299:             case DENIED:\n300:                 // logIfDenied is true if access to the resource was explicitly requested. Since this is an attempt\n301:                 // to access unauthorized resources, log at info level. If false, this is either a request to determine\n302:                 // authorized operations or a filter (e.g for regex subscriptions) to filter out authorized resources.\n303:                 // In this case, log only at trace level.\n304:                 if (action.logIfDenied()) {\n305:                     auditLog.info(buildAuditMessage(principal, requestContext, action, rule));\n306: }\n311: \n312:     private MatchingRule findAclRule(\n313:         Set<KafkaPrincipal> matchingPrincipals,\n314:         String host,\n315:         Action action\n316:     ) {\n317:         // This code relies on the ordering of StandardAcl within the NavigableMap.\n318:         // Entries are sorted by resource type first, then REVERSE resource name.\n319:         // Therefore, we can find all the applicable ACLs by starting at\n320:         // (resource_type, resource_name) and stepping forwards until we reach\n321:         // an ACL with a resource name which is not a prefix of the current one.\n322:         // At that point, we need to search for if there are any more ACLs at\n323:         // the first divergence point.\n324:         //\n325:         // For example, when trying to authorize a TOPIC resource named foobar, we would\n326:         // start at element 2, and continue on to 3 and 4 following map:\n327:         //\n328:         // 1. rs=TOPIC rn=gar pt=PREFIX\n329:         // 2. rs=TOPIC rn=foobar pt=PREFIX\n330:         // 3. rs=TOPIC rn=foob pt=LITERAL\n331:         // 4. rs=TOPIC rn=foo pt=PREFIX\n332:         // 5. rs=TOPIC rn=fb pt=PREFIX\n333:         // 6. rs=TOPIC rn=fa pt=PREFIX\n334:         // 7. rs=TOPIC rn=f  pt=PREFIX\n335:         // 8. rs=TOPIC rn=eeee pt=LITERAL\n336:         //\n337:         // Once we reached element 5, we would jump to element 7.\n338:         MatchingRuleBuilder matchingRuleBuilder = new MatchingRuleBuilder(noAclRule);\n339:         StandardAcl exemplar = new StandardAcl(\n340:             action.resourcePattern().resourceType(),\n341:             action.resourcePattern().name(),\n342:             PatternType.UNKNOWN, // Note that the UNKNOWN value sorts before all others.\n343:             \"\",\n344:             \"\",\n345:             AclOperation.UNKNOWN,\n346:             AclPermissionType.UNKNOWN);\n347:         AclCache aclCacheSnapshot = aclCache;\n348:         checkSection(aclCacheSnapshot, action, exemplar, matchingPrincipals, host, matchingRuleBuilder);\n349:         if (matchingRuleBuilder.foundDeny()) {\n350:             return matchingRuleBuilder.build();\n351:         }\n352: \n353:         // In addition to ACLs for this specific resource name, there can also be wildcard\n354:         // ACLs that match any resource name. These are stored as type = LITERAL,\n355:         // name = \"*\". We search these next.\n356:         exemplar = new StandardAcl(\n357:             action.resourcePattern().resourceType(),\n358:             WILDCARD,\n359:             LITERAL,\n360:             \"\",\n361:             \"\",\n362:             AclOperation.UNKNOWN,\n363:             AclPermissionType.UNKNOWN);\n364:         checkSection(aclCacheSnapshot, action, exemplar, matchingPrincipals, host, matchingRuleBuilder);\n365:         return matchingRuleBuilder.build();\n366:     }\n367: \n368:     static int matchesUpTo(\n369:         String resource,\n370:         String pattern\n371:     ) {\n372:         int i = 0;\n373:         while (true) {\n374:             if (resource.length() == i) break;\n375:             if (pattern.length() == i) break;\n376:             if (resource.charAt(i) != pattern.charAt(i)) break;\n377:             i++;\n378:         }\n379:         return i;\n380:     }\n381: \n382:     private void checkSection(\n383:             AclCache aclCacheSnapshot, Action action,\n384:             StandardAcl exemplar,\n385:             Set<KafkaPrincipal> matchingPrincipals,\n386:             String host,\n387:             MatchingRuleBuilder matchingRuleBuilder\n388:     ) {\n389:         String resourceName = action.resourcePattern().name();\n390:         NavigableSet<StandardAcl> tailSet =
